     <p>The <b>University of Pittsburgh</b> (commonly referred to as <b>Pitt</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Commonwealth System of Higher Education">state-related</a><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> research university located in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, United States. Founded as Pittsburgh Academy in 1787 on what was then the American frontier, Pitt is one of the oldest continuously chartered institutions of higher education in the United States. Pitt evolved into the Western University of Pennsylvania with an alteration to its charter in 1819, and upon relocating to its current campus in the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a> neighborhood of Pittsburgh in 1908, the school received its current moniker, the University of Pittsburgh. For most of its history Pitt was a private institution, until it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Commonwealth System of Higher Education">Commonwealth System of Higher Education</a> in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.9319871_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.9319871-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt has consistently placed in the top cluster of U.S. public research universities and among the overall top 25 research universities according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-TheCenterRankings_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheCenterRankings-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> is listed as one of <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a>'</i>s top 20 public universities,<sup id="cite_ref-usnews2010public_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usnews2010public-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> and has been listed among the best colleges for the quality of life of its students.<sup id="cite_ref-Mucha_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mucha-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt has also been named as a &quot;best value&quot; by various publications,<sup id="cite_ref-USNewsBV_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNewsBV-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KiplingerBV_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KiplingerBV-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PRbestvalue_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRbestvalue-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> and has appeared in multiple rankings of the world's top universities.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THE_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THE-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GUR_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GUR-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HEEACT_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEEACT-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt is among the nation's and world's most active research institutions as evidenced by its $899&nbsp;million in annual research expenditures, its receipt of the fifth largest amount of federally sponsored research funding among U.S. universities, and its election as one of the 62 North American members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NSFResearchBrief2011_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSFResearchBrief2011-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2009_Chancellor_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Chancellor-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt and its <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine">medical school</a> are also closely affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a>, one of the nation's leading academic medical centers.<sup id="cite_ref-UT_UPMC_HonorRoll_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UT_UPMC_HonorRoll-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt is popularly recognized for its centerpiece building, the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, for its central role in developing the first polio vaccine,<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.9319872_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.9319872-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> and for fielding nationally competitive <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">athletic programs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN.com_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN.com-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table id="toc" class="toc">

       <tr> 
        <td> 
         <div id="toctitle"> 
          <h2>Contents</h2> 
         </div> 
         <ul>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Brackenridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Brackenridge.jpg/170px-Brackenridge.jpg" width="170" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Brackenridge.jpg/255px-Brackenridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/55/Brackenridge.jpg/340px-Brackenridge.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Brackenridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Henry_Brackenridge" title="Hugh Henry Brackenridge">Hugh Henry Brackenridge</a>, founder of Pittsburgh Academy, the precursor to the University of Pittsburgh
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh" title="History of the University of Pittsburgh">History of the University of Pittsburgh</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding">Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Founded by <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Henry_Brackenridge" title="Hugh Henry Brackenridge">Hugh Henry Brackenridge</a> as <b>Pittsburgh Academy</b> in 1787, the University of Pittsburgh is one of the few universities and colleges established in the 18th century in the United States. It is the oldest continuously chartered institution of learning in the U.S. west of the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Mountains" title="Allegheny Mountains">Allegheny Mountains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The school began its life as a preparatory school, presumably in a <a href="/wiki/Log_Cabin_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Log Cabin (University of Pittsburgh)">log cabin</a>, possibly as early as 1770<sup id="cite_ref-Annual_catalog_of_the_Western_University_of_Pennsylvania.2C_Year_Ending_1905_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Annual_catalog_of_the_Western_University_of_Pennsylvania.2C_Year_Ending_1905-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> in Western Pennsylvania, then a frontier.<sup id="cite_ref-Early_Schools_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Early_Schools-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Hugh Henry Brackenridge sought and obtained a charter for the school from the state legislature of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Commonwealth of Pennsylvania</a> that was passed by the assembly on February 28, 1787, just ten weeks before the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Convention" title="Philadelphia Convention" class="mw-redirect">Constitutional Convention</a> in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-The_history_of_Pittsburgh:_its_rise_and_progress_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_history_of_Pittsburgh:_its_rise_and_progress-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Through_one_hundred_and_fifty_years:_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Through_one_hundred_and_fifty_years:_the_University_of_Pittsburgh-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> A brick building was erected in 1790 on the south side of Third Street and Cherry Alley for the Pittsburgh Academy.<sup id="cite_ref-owl1909_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1909-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-owl1910_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1910-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alberts_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alberts-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The small two-story brick building, with a gable facing the alley, contained three rooms: one below and two above.<sup id="cite_ref-Rev._John_Taylor:_the_first_rector_of_Trinity_Episcopal_Church_of_Pittsburgh_and_his_commonplace_book_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rev._John_Taylor:_the_first_rector_of_Trinity_Episcopal_Church_of_Pittsburgh_and_his_commonplace_book-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Western_University">The Western University</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Western University">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pitt1833.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/Pitt1833.jpg/220px-Pitt1833.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/Pitt1833.jpg/330px-Pitt1833.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ca/Pitt1833.jpg/440px-Pitt1833.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pitt1833.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University in 1833 at its location on 3rd Avenue in downtown Pittsburgh.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Within a short period, more advanced education in the area was needed, so in 1819 the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Commonwealth of Pennsylvania</a> amended the school's 1787 charter to confer university status. The school took the name the <b>Western University of Pennsylvania</b>, or WUP, and was intended to be the western sister institution to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Through_One_Hundred_and_Fifty_Years:_The_University_of_Pittsburgh_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Through_One_Hundred_and_Fifty_Years:_The_University_of_Pittsburgh-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Celebration_of_the_One_Hundred_and_Twenty-Fifth_Anniversary:_History_of_the_University_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Celebration_of_the_One_Hundred_and_Twenty-Fifth_Anniversary:_History_of_the_University-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1830, WUP had moved into a new three-story, freestone-fronted building, with Ionic columns and a cupola, near its original buildings fronting the south side of Third Street, between Smithfield Street and Cherry Alley in downtown <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>. By the 1830s, the university faced severe financial pressure to abandon its traditional liberal education in favor of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_General_Assembly" title="Pennsylvania General Assembly">state legislature's</a> desire for it to provide more vocational training. The decision to remain committed to liberal education nearly killed the university, but it persevered despite its abandonment by the city and state.<sup id="cite_ref-Alberts17_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alberts17-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also during this era that founder of <a href="/wiki/Mellon_Bank" title="Mellon Bank" class="mw-redirect">Mellon Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mellon" title="Thomas Mellon">Thomas Mellon</a> (Class of 1837), graduated and later taught at WUP.<sup id="cite_ref-owl1909_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1909-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-owl1910_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1910-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alberts_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alberts-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University's buildings, along with most of its records and files, were destroyed in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_Pittsburgh" title="Great Fire of Pittsburgh">Great Fire of 1845</a> that wiped out 20 square blocks of Pittsburgh. Classes were temporarily held in Trinity Church until a new building was constructed on Duquesne Way (on what was the site of the former <a href="/wiki/Horne%27s" title="Horne's" class="mw-redirect">Horne's</a> department store). Only four years later, in 1849, this building also was destroyed by fire. Due to the catastrophic nature of these fires, operations were suspended for a few years to allow the University time to regroup and rebuild. By 1854, WUP had erected a new building on the corner of Ross and Diamond (now Forbes Avenue) streets (site of the present day <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_City-County_Building" title="Pittsburgh City-County Building">City-County building</a>) and classes resumed in 1855. It is during this era, in 1867, that <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Pierpoint_Langley" title="Samuel Pierpoint Langley" class="mw-redirect">Samuel Pierpoint Langley</a>, astronomer, inventor, aviation pioneer and future Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a>, was chosen as director of the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Observatory" title="Allegheny Observatory">Allegheny Observatory</a> that was donated to WUP in 1865. Langley was professor of astronomy and physics and remained at WUP until 1891, when he was succeeded by another prominent astronomer, <a href="/wiki/James_Edward_Keeler" title="James Edward Keeler">James Keeler</a>. Growing quickly during this period, WUP outgrew its downtown facilities and the university moved its campus to <a href="/wiki/Allegheny,_Pennsylvania" title="Allegheny, Pennsylvania">Allegheny City</a> (present-day <a href="/wiki/Northside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Northside (Pittsburgh)" class="mw-redirect">North Side</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-owl1909_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1909-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-owl1910_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1910-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alberts_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alberts-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pitt1890to1909.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/31/Pitt1890to1909.jpg/220px-Pitt1890to1909.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/31/Pitt1890to1909.jpg/330px-Pitt1890to1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/31/Pitt1890to1909.jpg/440px-Pitt1890to1909.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pitt1890to1909.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Observatory Hill campus on Pittsburgh's North Side from 1890 to 1909
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University eventually found itself on a 10-acre (4.0&nbsp;ha) site on the North Side's <a href="/wiki/Observatory_Hill_(Pittsburgh)" title="Observatory Hill (Pittsburgh)" class="mw-redirect">Observatory Hill</a> at the location of its <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Observatory" title="Allegheny Observatory">Allegheny Observatory</a>. There, it constructed two new buildings, Science Hall and Main Hall, that were occupied by 1889 and 1890 respectively. During this era, the first collegiate football team was formed at Pitt in 1889. In 1892, the Western Pennsylvania Medical College was amalgamated into the University. By 1893, the University had graduated its first African-American, William Dammond.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_History_.E2.80.93_1893:_William_Hunter_Dammond_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_History_.E2.80.93_1893:_William_Hunter_Dammond-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1895, WUP established its School of Law and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Westinghouse" title="George Westinghouse">George Westinghouse</a> were elected to the Board of Trustees, where they joined <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Mellon" title="Andrew Mellon" class="mw-redirect">Andrew Mellon</a> who was elected in 1894. The Pittsburgh College of Pharmacy and Pittsburgh Dental School also joined the University in 1896. In 1898, the first women, sisters Margaret and Stella Stein, graduated from the University.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_History_.E2.80.93_1898:_Margaret_and_Stella_Stein_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_History_.E2.80.93_1898:_Margaret_and_Stella_Stein-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> During this period, University engineering professor <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Fessenden" title="Reginald Fessenden">Reginald Fessenden</a> was conducting pioneering work in radio broadcasting. By 1904, playing at <a href="/wiki/Exposition_Park_(Pittsburgh)" title="Exposition Park (Pittsburgh)">Exposition Park</a>, the University had its first undefeated football team.<sup id="cite_ref-owl1909_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1909-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-owl1910_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owl1910-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alberts_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alberts-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_History_.E2.80.93_1906:_Reginald_Fessenden_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_History_.E2.80.93_1906:_Reginald_Fessenden-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A_new_name_and_home">A new name and home</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: A new name and home">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg/170px-Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg" width="170" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg/255px-Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg/340px-Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_Learning_stitch_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, the centerpiece of Pitt's campus and the tallest educational building in the Western Hemisphere
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Citing a need to avoid confusion, distinguish itself from the University of Pennsylvania, and return to its roots by identifying itself with the city, the Western University of Pennsylvania, by act of the state legislature, was renamed the <b>University of Pittsburgh</b> in the summer of 1908. During this time, the University had also outgrown its accommodations on what is now the North Side of Pittsburgh and its departments had been scattered throughout the city for years. To consolidate all of its components on one campus, WUP bought 43 acres (170,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of land in December 1907 in what is now the Oakland neighborhood of Pittsburgh and began relocating departments there by 1909.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Owl_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Owl-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The initial campus plan for the new location centered on the winning submission from a national architectural contest that incorporated a Greek Acropolis design by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hornbostel" title="Henry Hornbostel">Henry Hornbostel</a> for 30 buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_the_story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh.2C_1787.E2.80.931987_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_the_story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh.2C_1787.E2.80.931987-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> However, due to financial and other constraints, only four of the buildings were constructed in this style, of which only <a href="/wiki/Thaw_Hall" title="Thaw Hall">Thaw Hall</a> remains today. In the fall of 1909, the University became the first college to adopt the <a href="/wiki/Panthers_of_Pittsburgh" title="Panthers of Pittsburgh">panther</a> as its mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Panther_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Panther-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also during this period that the university, led by Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Samuel_McCormick" title="Samuel McCormick">Samuel McCormick</a>, would again fend off pressures to abandon the school's commitment to liberal education in favor of more technical-based training. During his administration, McCormick would also lead the university into a new level of national recognition, expansion, and growth, as well as began institutional support of athletics.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.9319873_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.9319873-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 1920s, new university chancellor <a href="/wiki/John_Gabbert_Bowman" title="John Gabbert Bowman">John Gabbert Bowman</a> declared that he had a vision for a centerpiece &quot;tall building&quot; for the university. The 14 acres (5.7&nbsp;ha) Frick Acres property in Oakland was soon purchased and plans for the campus shifted focus from the hillside to a neo-<a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a> plan that today comprises the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Memorial Chapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster_Memorial" title="Stephen Foster Memorial">Stephen Foster Memorial</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clapp_Hall" title="Clapp Hall">Clapp Hall</a> buildings. By 1925, Bowman had settled on a design by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Klauder" title="Charles Klauder">Charles Klauder</a> for the &quot;tall building&quot;: an attention-getting 535-foot (163&nbsp;m) tower whose great height, with open spaces all around, would suggest the &quot;character that ought to be in an educated man.&quot; The building's &quot;parallel lines going up and up...would express courage [and] fearlessness&quot; and it would &quot;unify Pittsburgh into a community conscious of its character.&quot; The Cathedral is &quot;cut off&quot; flat at the top to suggest that its lines, like education, have no ending. The building was financed by donors as well as a campaign to collect dimes from local school children. Bowman was a persuasive leader and although the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> intervened, the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, on which construction was begun in 1926, started hosting classes in 1931 and was formally dedicated in 1937. Today, it remains the second tallest university building in the world and contains an equally-impressive interior highlighted by a half-acre (2,000 m&sup2;) Gothic hall Commons Room with 52-foot (16&nbsp;m) tall arches currently surrounded by 29&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Nationality_Rooms" title="Nationality Rooms">Nationality Rooms</a>, however seven more Nationality Rooms are in the making.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Nationality_Rooms_-_rooms_in_planning_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Nationality_Rooms_-_rooms_in_planning-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_the_polio_vaccine">Development of the polio vaccine</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Development of the polio vaccine">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:SalkatPitt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/SalkatPitt.jpg/170px-SalkatPitt.jpg" width="170" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ca/SalkatPitt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ca/SalkatPitt.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:SalkatPitt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Salk" title="Jonas Salk">Jonas Salk</a> developed the first polio vaccine at the University of Pittsburgh.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the early 20th century, epidemics of <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a> began to hit the United States and other industrialized countries. As hospital wards filled with patients in <a href="/wiki/Negative_pressure_ventilator" title="Negative pressure ventilator">iron lungs</a>, and tens of thousands were left disabled, fear of contracting polio grew rampant and led to the closing of many public facilities. Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Salk" title="Jonas Salk">Dr. Jonas Salk</a> had set up the University of Pittsburgh's Virus Research Lab in the basement of what is now <a href="/wiki/Salk_Hall" title="Salk Hall">Salk Hall</a>. By 1951, Salk and his team had begun immunization experiments in monkeys using dead polio virus. Soon, however, Salk began to test inoculations in paralyzed polio patients and by 1953 human trials among the general population were initiated. By the spring of the following year, the largest controlled field trials in medical history were underway, and by 1955 the <a href="/wiki/Polio_vaccine" title="Polio vaccine">vaccine</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Salk" title="Jonas Salk">Jonas Salk</a> and his team of Pitt researchers was declared effective. By 1962, Salk's vaccine had reduced the incidence of polio in the United States by <i>95 percent</i>. The breakthroughs in immunology and vaccine development at Pitt by Salk and his team are considered one of the most significant scientific and medical achievements in history.<sup id="cite_ref-Remembering_Polio:_Celebrating_the_50th_Anniversary_of_the_Salk_Polio_Vaccine_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Remembering_Polio:_Celebrating_the_50th_Anniversary_of_the_Salk_Polio_Vaccine-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Shot_Heard_.27Round_the_World_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Shot_Heard_.27Round_the_World-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_relations_to_present_day">State relations to present day</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: State relations to present day">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1966, Pitt was designated by <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Commonwealth System of Higher Education">state-related</a> university. As such, Pitt receives public funds ($185.4&nbsp;million in fiscal year 2011) covering about 9% of its operating budget and offers reduced tuition to Pennsylvania residents. Pitt remains under independent control, but is typically categorized as a public university. Upon affiliation with the state, subsidized tuition led to a massive influx of new students and rapid expansion of Pitt's size and scope. In the 1970s, Pitt's football team returned to greatness with a national championship season in 1976 led by <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> running back <a href="/wiki/Tony_Dorsett" title="Tony Dorsett">Tony Dorsett</a> and continued success in the 1980s with players such as <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> quarterback <a href="/wiki/Dan_Marino" title="Dan Marino">Dan Marino</a>. In the 1980s, significant medical research in the field of <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplantation" title="Organ transplantation">organ transplantation</a> was conducted by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Starzl" title="Thomas Starzl">Thomas Starzl</a>, establishing Pitt as the world leader in the field of organ transplantation. In 1991, long-time chancellor <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Posvar" title="Wesley Posvar">Wesley Posvar</a> retired after 24 years in office. His administration is best known for elimination of the university's debt from its 1960s financial crisis and for increasing the school's prestige and endowment. Under Posvar, Pitt's operating budget grew sevenfold to $630&nbsp;million and its endowment tripled to $257&nbsp;million.<sup id="cite_ref-pitt_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitt-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Mark_Nordenberg" title="Mark Nordenberg">Mark Nordenberg</a> has been chancellor of the University since 1995 and is leading Pitt through a period of substantial progress, including a $2-billion capital-raising campaign that is over three quarters of the way toward achieving its goal<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Giving:_Office_of_Institutional_Advancement_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Giving:_Office_of_Institutional_Advancement-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> and a $1-billion 12-year facilities plan.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Announces_12-Year_Facilities_Plan_To_Support_Programmatic_Direction_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Announces_12-Year_Facilities_Plan_To_Support_Programmatic_Direction-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Major initiatives and events that have occurred during his tenure include the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Petersen_Events_Center" title="Petersen Events Center">Petersen Events Center</a>, a major expansion of on-campus housing, the growth of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a> and the restructuring of its relationship with the university, a series of <a href="/wiki/2012_University_of_Pittsburgh_bomb_threats" title="2012 University of Pittsburgh bomb threats">disruptive bomb threats</a> that occurred in 2012, and the growth of Pitt's endowment to its current value of $2.618&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Endowment_FY2012_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Endowment_FY2012-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:HeinzChapelSouth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/HeinzChapelSouth.jpg/220px-HeinzChapelSouth.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/HeinzChapelSouth.jpg/330px-HeinzChapelSouth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/HeinzChapelSouth.jpg/440px-HeinzChapelSouth.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:HeinzChapelSouth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Memorial Chapel</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Pittsburgh's main campus comprises approximately 132 urban acres (0.53&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) located in Pittsburgh's historic <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a> neighborhood. Much of the campus, including its centerpiece 42-story <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, falls within the <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Farms_Historic_District" title="Schenley Farms Historic District">Oakland Civic Center/Schenley Farms National Historic District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP-districts_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-districts-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus contains an eclectic mix of architecture that includes Greek revival, Neogothic, Italian Renaissance, and modern. It has been termed &quot;a theme park of replica buildings, representing the architecture of the past speaking to the present.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Weighing_in_on_Pitt.27s_eclectic_architecture_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weighing_in_on_Pitt.27s_eclectic_architecture-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus has won multiple Green Star Awards from the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Grounds_Management_Society" title="Professional Grounds Management Society">Professional Grounds Management Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Wins_Grounds_Services_Award_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Wins_Grounds_Services_Award-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PGMS_Green_Star_Awards:_Urban_University_Grounds:_University_of_Pittsburgh_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PGMS_Green_Star_Awards:_Urban_University_Grounds:_University_of_Pittsburgh-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PGMS_News_-_PGMS_Salutes_Grounds_Management_Excellence.3B_College_and_University_Grounds_Lead_the_Way_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PGMS_News_-_PGMS_Salutes_Grounds_Management_Excellence.3B_College_and_University_Grounds_Lead_the_Way-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Pittsburgh's main campus can be thought to be made up of four contiguous sections: upper (sports complexes, <a href="/wiki/Upper_campus_residence_halls_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Upper campus residence halls (University of Pittsburgh)">residence halls</a>); mid (<a href="/wiki/Benedum_Hall" title="Benedum Hall">Benedum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Science_Center" title="Chevron Science Center">Chevron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Hall_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Allen Hall (University of Pittsburgh)">Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thaw_Hall" title="Thaw Hall">Thaw Halls</a>); lower (<a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wesley_W._Posvar_Hall" title="Wesley W. Posvar Hall">Posvar Hall</a>); and on the west end of campus, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">medical center complex</a>. The campus is generally bordered by Darragh Street/McKee Place to the west and Bellefield Avenue/Dithridge Street to the east; Forbes and Fifth avenues traverse the campus from west to east. Although generally within walking distance, the university also runs a <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Transportation_System" title="University of Pittsburgh Transportation System">bus and shuttle service</a> between various campus locations and bordering neighborhoods.</p> 
     <p>The main campus abuts or is within a short walking distance of many recreational, cultural, and educational institutions that also populate the Oakland neighborhood. The campus is directly adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Plaza" title="Schenley Plaza">Schenley Plaza</a>, the main branch of the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Library_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Public Library</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Museums of Natural History and Art</a>, and the Carnegie Music Hall. <a href="/wiki/Carlow_University" title="Carlow University">Carlow University</a> is just west of campus, adjacent to the University's medical center complexes. <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Catholic_High_School_(Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania)" title="Central Catholic High School (Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania)" class="mw-redirect">Central Catholic High School</a> and historic <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Park" title="Schenley Park">Schenley Park</a>, site of the <a href="/wiki/Phipps_Conservatory_%26_Botanical_Gardens" title="Phipps Conservatory &amp; Botanical Gardens">Phipps Conservatory &amp; Botanical Gardens</a>, lie across <a href="/wiki/Junction_Hollow" title="Junction Hollow">Junction Hollow</a> on the east end. Some Pitt professors also hold adjunct professorships at Carnegie Mellon and <i>vice-versa</i>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_buildings">Historic buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Historic buildings">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:StephenFosterWinter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/StephenFosterWinter.jpg/220px-StephenFosterWinter.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/StephenFosterWinter.jpg/330px-StephenFosterWinter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/StephenFosterWinter.jpg/440px-StephenFosterWinter.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:StephenFosterWinter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster_Memorial" title="Stephen Foster Memorial">Stephen Foster Memorial</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>There are two University buildings listed separately on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>: <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Observatory" title="Allegheny Observatory">Allegheny Observatory</a> (in Pittsburgh's Riverview Park on the <a href="/wiki/Northside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Northside (Pittsburgh)" class="mw-redirect">Northside</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PENNSYLVANIA_.E2.80.93_Allegheny_County_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PENNSYLVANIA_.E2.80.93_Allegheny_County-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Twenty-one of Pitt's buildings (including the 5 residence halls that make up <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Quadrangle" title="Schenley Quadrangle">Schenley Quadrangle</a>, see below) are <a href="/wiki/Contributing_properties" title="Contributing properties" class="mw-redirect">contributing properties</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Farms_Historic_District" title="Schenley Farms Historic District">Schenley Farms-Oakland Civic Center Historic District</a> that has been listed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Historic_district_(United_States)" title="Historic district (United States)" class="mw-redirect">historic district</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NRHP-districts_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRHP-districts-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Due to the historical nature of various sites in or around Pitt's buildings, the Commonwealth of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> has placed historical markers outside the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Observatory" title="Allegheny Observatory">Allegheny Observatory</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Marker_Details:_Allegheny_Observatory_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marker_Details:_Allegheny_Observatory-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wesley_W._Posvar_Hall" title="Wesley W. Posvar Hall">Posvar Hall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Marker_Details:_Forbes_Field_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marker_Details:_Forbes_Field-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Marker_Details:_Barney_Dreyfuss_.281865-1932.29_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marker_Details:_Barney_Dreyfuss_.281865-1932.29-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Salk_Hall" title="Salk Hall">Salk Hall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Salk_Polio_Vaccine_.E2.80.93_Pennsylvania_Historical_Markers_on_Waymarking.com_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salk_Polio_Vaccine_.E2.80.93_Pennsylvania_Historical_Markers_on_Waymarking.com-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster_Memorial" title="Stephen Foster Memorial">Stephen Foster Memorial</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Stephen_C._Foster_Memorial_.E2.80.93_Pennsylvania_Historical_Markers_on_Waymarking.com_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stephen_C._Foster_Memorial_.E2.80.93_Pennsylvania_Historical_Markers_on_Waymarking.com-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">William Pitt Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-V.F.W._.E2.80.93_Pennsylvania_Historical_Markers_on_Waymarking.com_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V.F.W._.E2.80.93_Pennsylvania_Historical_Markers_on_Waymarking.com-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, a Pennsylvania Historical Marker has been placed on campus near the Cathedral of Learning to mark the significance of the University of Pittsburgh itself.<sup id="cite_ref-Marker_Details:_University_of_Pittsburgh_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marker_Details:_University_of_Pittsburgh-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Another state historical marker has been placed to highlight the significance of Pitt's involvement in the archaeological excavation at the <a href="/wiki/Meadowcroft_Rockshelter" title="Meadowcroft Rockshelter">Meadowcroft Rockshelter</a> in <a href="/wiki/Avella,_Pennsylvania" title="Avella, Pennsylvania">Avella, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marker_Details:_Meadowcroft_Rockshelter_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marker_Details:_Meadowcroft_Rockshelter-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_History_and_Landmarks_Foundation" title="Pittsburgh History and Landmarks Foundation">Pittsburgh History and Landmarks Foundation</a> has designated the following Pitt buildings as Pittsburgh Historic Landmarks: <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Observatory" title="Allegheny Observatory">Allegheny Observatory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Hall_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Allen Hall (University of Pittsburgh)">Allen Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alumni_Hall_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Alumni Hall (University of Pittsburgh)">Alumni Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellefield_Hall" title="Bellefield Hall">Bellefield Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chancellor%27s_Residence_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Chancellor's Residence (University of Pittsburgh)">Chancellor's Residence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning#Commons_Room" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning interior rooms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gardner_Steel_Conference_Center" title="Gardner Steel Conference Center">Gardner Steel Conference Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Memorial Chapel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thaw_Hall" title="Thaw Hall">Thaw Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salk_Hall" title="Salk Hall">Salk Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Quadrangle" title="Schenley Quadrangle">Schenley Quadrangle residence halls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster_Memorial" title="Stephen Foster Memorial">Stephen Foster Memorial</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_Child_Development_Center" title="University Child Development Center">University Child Development Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">William Pitt Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_History_and_Landmarks_Foundation:_PHLF_Plaques_.26_Registries_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh_History_and_Landmarks_Foundation:_PHLF_Plaques_.26_Registries-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_History_.26_Landmarks_Foundation_announces_Historic_Building_and_Landscape_Designations_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh_History_.26_Landmarks_Foundation_announces_Historic_Building_and_Landscape_Designations-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Other Pitt buildings not designated individually as landmarks, but listed among the 16 Pitt-owned contributing properties to the Schenley Farms Historic District, include <a href="/wiki/Clapp_Hall" title="Clapp Hall">Clapp Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/O%27Hara_Student_Center" title="O'Hara Student Center">O'Hara Student Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruskin_Hall" title="Ruskin Hall">Ruskin Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thackeray_Hall" title="Thackeray Hall">Thackeray Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frick_Fine_Arts_Building" title="Frick Fine Arts Building">Frick Fine Arts Building</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_Building_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Music Building (University of Pittsburgh)">Music Building</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_Club_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="University Club (University of Pittsburgh)">University Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hearing_set_on_historic_landmark_nomination_for_two_Pitt_buildings_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hearing_set_on_historic_landmark_nomination_for_two_Pitt_buildings-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Historic structures within, adjacent to, or near Pitt's campus, but not belonging to the university, include the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Museum buildings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Science_and_Technology_Academy" title="Pittsburgh Science and Technology Academy">Frick School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Field" title="Forbes Field">Forbes Field</a> wall remnant, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Magee_(politician)" title="Christopher Magee (politician)">Magee</a> Estate iron fence, the <a href="/wiki/Mary_Schenley_Memorial_Fountain" title="Mary Schenley Memorial Fountain">Schenley Fountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mellon_Institute" title="Mellon Institute" class="mw-redirect">Mellon Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phipps_Conservatory_%26_Botanical_Gardens" title="Phipps Conservatory &amp; Botanical Gardens">Phipps Conservatory &amp; Botanical Gardens</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Athletic_Association" title="Pittsburgh Athletic Association">Pittsburgh Athletic Association</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Saint_Paul_in_Pittsburgh" title="Cathedral of Saint Paul in Pittsburgh" class="mw-redirect">St. Paul's Cathedral</a>, St. Nicholas Greek Orthodox Church, <a href="/wiki/Schenley_High_School" title="Schenley High School">Schenley High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soldiers_and_Sailors_Memorial_Hall" title="Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Hall" class="mw-redirect">Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Hall</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster_(sculpture)" title="Stephen Foster (sculpture)">Stephen Foster sculpture</a>. Many of these buildings and their facilities are integrated into the events and activities of the university.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_buildings">Other buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other buildings">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Pittsburgh_buildings" title="List of University of Pittsburgh buildings">List of University of Pittsburgh buildings</a>
     </div>

      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

     <p>The majority of <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Pittsburgh_buildings" title="List of University of Pittsburgh buildings">Pitt-owned facilities</a> are clustered in the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a> neighborhood of Pittsburgh which includes the <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Farms_Historic_District" title="Schenley Farms Historic District">Schenley Farms Historic District</a>, however a few prominent facilities are scattered elsewhere throughout the city, including the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Shadyside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Shadyside (Pittsburgh)">Shadyside</a> neighborhood. Pitt also maintains regional Pennsylvania campuses in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Bradford" title="University of Pittsburgh at Bradford">Bradford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Greensburg" title="University of Pittsburgh at Greensburg">Greensburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Johnstown" title="University of Pittsburgh at Johnstown">Johnstown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Titusville" title="University of Pittsburgh at Titusville">Titusville</a>, as well as a Computer Center in RIDC Park in <a href="/wiki/Blawnox,_Pennsylvania" title="Blawnox, Pennsylvania">Blawnox</a>, the Plum Boro Science Center in <a href="/wiki/Plum,_Pennsylvania" title="Plum, Pennsylvania">Plum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Applied_Research_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Applied Research Center">University of Pittsburgh Applied Research Center</a> (U-PARC) in <a href="/wiki/Harmarville,_Pennsylvania" title="Harmarville, Pennsylvania">Harmarville</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pymatuning_Laboratory_of_Ecology" title="Pymatuning Laboratory of Ecology">Pymatuning Laboratory of Ecology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Linesville,_Pennsylvania" title="Linesville, Pennsylvania">Linesville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Pymatuning_Laboratory_of_Ecology_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Pymatuning_Laboratory_of_Ecology-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also has a major archeological research site, the <a href="/wiki/Allen_L._Cook_Spring_Creek_Preserve" title="Allen L. Cook Spring Creek Preserve">Allen L. Cook Spring Creek Preserve</a>, in Spring Creek, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Honors_College_Receives_4.2C700_Acres_of_Wyoming_Land_Teeming_With_Dinosaur_Fossils_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Honors_College_Receives_4.2C700_Acres_of_Wyoming_Land_Teeming_With_Dinosaur_Fossils-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Go_West_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Go_West-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Athletic facilities of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Panthers" title="University of Pittsburgh Panthers" class="mw-redirect">University of Pittsburgh Panthers</a> that are located in Oakland in the upper campus and include the <a href="/wiki/Cost_Sports_Center" title="Cost Sports Center">Charles L Cost Sports Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fitzgerald_Field_House" title="Fitzgerald Field House">Fitzgerald Field House</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Petersen_Events_Center" title="Petersen Events Center">Petersen Events Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trees_Hall" title="Trees Hall">Trees Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/File:TreesField3.jpg" title="File:TreesField3.jpg">Trees Field</a>. An approximately $30&nbsp;million upgrade of on-campus sports facilities, starting with the <a href="/wiki/Petersen_Sports_Complex" title="Petersen Sports Complex">Petersen Sports Complex</a>, includes new soccer, baseball, softball facilities, and helps clear a space for the future construction of a new track and field and band complex.<sup id="cite_ref-Petersen_Sports_Complex_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petersen_Sports_Complex-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Athletic facilities in Pittsburgh that are located outside of the Oakland neighborhood include <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UPMC_Sports_Performance_Complex" title="UPMC Sports Performance Complex">UPMC Sports Performance Complex</a>.</p> 
     <p>Major on-campus residence halls include the <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_Towers" title="Litchfield Towers">Litchfield Towers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Quadrangle" title="Schenley Quadrangle">Schenley Quadrangle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bouquet_Gardens" title="Bouquet Gardens">Bouquet Gardens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruskin_Hall" title="Ruskin Hall">Ruskin Hall</a> located on the lower campus, <a href="/wiki/Lothrop_Hall" title="Lothrop Hall">Lothrop Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Hall" title="Forbes Hall">Forbes Hall</a> on the medical campus, and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Hall_(Pittsburgh)" title="Pennsylvania Hall (Pittsburgh)" class="mw-redirect">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panther_Hall" title="Panther Hall" class="mw-redirect">Panther</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sutherland_Hall" title="Sutherland Hall" class="mw-redirect">Sutherland</a> halls located on the upper campus.</p>

      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WPUlawn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/WPUlawn.jpg/220px-WPUlawn.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/WPUlawn.jpg/330px-WPUlawn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/WPUlawn.jpg/440px-WPUlawn.jpg 2x" /></a>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Pittsburgh_buildings#UPMC" title="List of University of Pittsburgh buildings">List of UPMC buildings in Pittsburgh</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a> (UPMC), which is consistently ranked in U.S. News &amp; World Report's &quot;Honor Roll&quot; of America's top hospitals,<sup id="cite_ref-UPMCrank_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPMCrank-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> consists of the following hospitals and facilities in the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a> area, many of which have shared use with various university departments: UPMC Presbyterian Hospital, UPMC Montefiore Hospital, Magee-Women's Hospital of UPMC, Western Psychiatric Institute and Clinic in Thomas Detre Hall, Eye and Ear Institute, <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Tower" title="Forbes Tower">Forbes Tower</a> (home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Health_and_Rehabilitation_Sciences" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences">School of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences</a>), Iroquois Building, Kaufman Medical Building, Medical Arts Building, 230 McKee Place, and UPMC University Center. UPMC academic hospitals and facilities that are scattered elsewhere throughout the city include the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_of_Pittsburgh_of_UPMC" title="Children's Hospital of Pittsburgh of UPMC">Children's Hospital of Pittsburgh of UPMC</a> campus in the <a href="/wiki/Lawrenceville_(Pittsburgh)" title="Lawrenceville (Pittsburgh)">Lawrencevville</a> neighborhood, the <a href="/wiki/UPMC_Sports_Performance_Complex" title="UPMC Sports Performance Complex">UPMC Sports Performance Complex</a> on the <a href="/wiki/South_Side_(Pittsburgh)" title="South Side (Pittsburgh)">South Side</a>, and UPMC Shadyside and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Cancer_Institute" title="University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute">University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute</a> in the Hillman Cancer Center both located in the <a href="/wiki/Shadyside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Shadyside (Pittsburgh)">Shadyside</a> neighborhood adjacent to Oakland.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_campuses">Regional campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Regional campuses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Regional campuses offer Master's, Bachelor's, and <a href="/wiki/Associate%27s_degree" title="Associate's degree" class="mw-redirect">Associate's</a> degrees at four locations in <a href="/wiki/Western_Pennsylvania" title="Western Pennsylvania">Western Pennsylvania</a>. They also allow students to take preliminary courses and relocate to other regional campuses or the Oakland campus to complete their degrees. They offer several degrees and certificates:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Bradford" title="University of Pittsburgh at Bradford">University of Pittsburgh at Bradford</a> – Master's, Bachelor's, Associate's and Certificate</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Greensburg" title="University of Pittsburgh at Greensburg">University of Pittsburgh at Greensburg</a> – Master's, Bachelor's and Certificate</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Johnstown" title="University of Pittsburgh at Johnstown">University of Pittsburgh at Johnstown</a> – Bachelor's and Certificate</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_at_Titusville" title="University of Pittsburgh at Titusville">University of Pittsburgh at Titusville</a> – Bachelor's in Business Management and Arts in Human Relations, Associate's and Certificate</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Community_impact">Community impact</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Community impact">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Eberlyhallside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Eberlyhallside.jpg/170px-Eberlyhallside.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Eberlyhallside.jpg/255px-Eberlyhallside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Eberlyhallside.jpg/340px-Eberlyhallside.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Eberlyhallside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Eberly_Hall" title="Eberly Hall">Eberly Hall</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Pittsburgh has been noted for both its role in community outreach and its impact on the economy of the city and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Pennsylvania" title="Western Pennsylvania">Western Pennsylvania</a> region. In 2009, Pitt was ranked second overall, and the top public university in the nation, as a &quot;Best Neighbor&quot; for positive impact on its urban community, including both commercial and residential activities such as revitalization, cultural renewal, economics, and community service and development according to the &quot;Saviors of Our Cities&quot; ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-Saviors_of_Our_Cities:_2009_Survey_of_College_.26_University_Civic_Partnerships_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saviors_of_Our_Cities:_2009_Survey_of_College_.26_University_Civic_Partnerships-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt was also listed as a &quot;best neighbor&quot; in the previous ranking released in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-CMU.2C_Pitt_rate_as_good_neighbors_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CMU.2C_Pitt_rate_as_good_neighbors-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> These rankings reflect the statistics that each year Pitt spends more than $1.7&nbsp;billion in the community and supports nearly 33,800&nbsp;jobs in <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Allegheny County, Pennsylvania">Allegheny County</a>. Pitt's research program alone imports more than $822&nbsp;million into the region each year (more than $3.60 for each $1 of state appropriations), and supports some 23,100 local jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-harvith_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvith-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chancellor_Mark_A._Nordenberg_Issues_a_University_Update_on_the_Economy_and_Our_Community_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chancellor_Mark_A._Nordenberg_Issues_a_University_Update_on_the_Economy_and_Our_Community-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_2008_Report_of_Chancellor_Mark_A._Nordenberg_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_2008_Report_of_Chancellor_Mark_A._Nordenberg-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt students also spend more than $213&nbsp;million on goods, services, and rental payments within the local economy.<sup id="cite_ref-chancellor-2006_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chancellor-2006-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt ranked sixth in the number of startups spawned by technologies developed by its researchers according to <a href="/wiki/Association_of_University_Technology_Managers" title="Association of University Technology Managers">Association of University Technology Managers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AUTM_U.S._Licensing_Survey.2C_FY_2004:_A_Survey_Summary_of_Technology_Licensing_.28and_Related.29_Performance_for_U.S._Academic_and_Nonprofit_Institutions.2C_and_Technology_Investment_firms_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AUTM_U.S._Licensing_Survey.2C_FY_2004:_A_Survey_Summary_of_Technology_Licensing_.28and_Related.29_Performance_for_U.S._Academic_and_Nonprofit_Institutions.2C_and_Technology_Investment_firms-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt and its <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine">medical school</a> are closely affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a>. With over 50,000 employees and more than $7&nbsp;billion in annual revenue, the Medical Center is the largest employer in Western Pennsylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-UPMC_Community_Benefits_Report_Fiscal_Year_2008:_Strengthening_the_Fabric_of_a_Community_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPMC_Community_Benefits_Report_Fiscal_Year_2008:_Strengthening_the_Fabric_of_a_Community-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Through the Pitt Volunteer Pool, faculty and staff members donate more than 10,000 hours annually to community service projects for agencies such as the Salvation Army, Pittsburgh AIDS Task Force, and Greater Pittsburgh Community Food Bank.</p> 
     <p>Pitt also is a leading producer of <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a> volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-chancellor-2006_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chancellor-2006-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-University_ranks_high_in_Peace_Corps_volunteers_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_ranks_high_in_Peace_Corps_volunteers-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Peace Corps' 2008 ranking of colleges and universities, only 14&nbsp;schools in the nation produced more Peace Corp volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-Peace_Corps_Top_Colleges_and_Universities_2008_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peace_Corps_Top_Colleges_and_Universities_2008-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt's graduate school also ranked 10th for most alumni Peace Corps volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-webster_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webster-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University was chartered by the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania in 1787 and it operated as a fully private institution until an alteration to its charter in 1966 at which point it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Commonwealth System of Higher Education">Commonwealth System of Higher Education</a>. This conferred &quot;state-related&quot; status to the university making it a legal instrument of the Commonwealth which provides an annual financial appropriation, currently 7.7% of the university's total operating budget,<sup id="cite_ref-budgetcuts_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-budgetcuts-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> in exchange for the university offering tuition discounts to students that are residents of Pennsylvania. Legally, however, the university remains a private entity, operating under its nonprofit corporate charter, governed by its independent Board of Trustees, and with its assets under its own ownership and control. Therefore it retains the freedom and individuality of a private institution, both administratively and academically, setting its own standards for admissions, awarding of degrees, faculty qualifications, teaching, and staff hiring.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University's Board of Trustees maintains ultimate legal authority, governance, and responsibility for the university but specifically reserves authority over the selection the university's Chancellor; approval of major policies, particularly those related to the fiduciary responsibilities of the Board; and the definition of the university's mission and goals. It is made up 36 voting members that include the Chancellor, 17 Term Trustees elected by the Board, six Alumni Trustees elected by the board on nomination from the Alumni Association Board of Directors, and 12 Commonwealth trustees. The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Pennsylvania" title="Governor of Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect">Governor of Pennsylvania</a>, the President Pro Tempore of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Senate" title="Pennsylvania Senate" class="mw-redirect">Pennsylvania Senate</a>, and the Speaker of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_House_of_Representatives" title="Pennsylvania House of Representatives">Pennsylvania House of Representatives</a> each appoint four of the 12 Commonwealth trustees. Additional non-voting trustees include 14 Special Trustees and additional Emeritus Trustees selected by the Board. Non-voting ex-officio members include the Governor of Pennsylvania, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Commonwealth_of_Pennsylvania" title="Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania">Secretary of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania</a>, the Chief Executive of <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Allegheny County, Pennsylvania">Allegheny County</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Pittsburgh" title="Mayor of Pittsburgh" class="mw-redirect">Mayor of Pittsburgh</a>. There are three or more regular meetings of the Board of Trustees per year.<sup id="cite_ref-Faculty_Handbook_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faculty_Handbook-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Board of Trustees selects the university's Chancellor, who doubles as the chief academic officer and the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_Officer" title="Chief Executive Officer" class="mw-redirect">Chief Executive Officer</a> of the university as well as serving as an ex officio voting member of the Board or Trustees. The Chancellor is delegated with general administrative, academic, and management authority over the university. Under the Chancellor are the Provost and Senior Vice Chancellor, the Senior Vice Chancellor for Health Sciences, the deans of the various schools, the presidents of the regional campuses, department chairs, and the directors of University centers and institutes.<sup id="cite_ref-Faculty_Handbook_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faculty_Handbook-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Bachelor's, master's, doctoral and professional programs are offered through the following schools and colleges:</p> 
     <table style="border:0 solid #ddd; background:#fefefe; padding:3px; margin:0;"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Dietrich_School_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Dietrich School of Arts and Sciences">Dietrich School of Arts and Sciences</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_M._Katz_School_of_Business" title="Joseph M. Katz School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Joseph M. Katz Graduate School of Business</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_College_of_Business_Administration" title="University of Pittsburgh College of Business Administration">College of Business Administration</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Dental Medicine">School of Dental Medicine</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Education" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Education">School of Education</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Swanson_School_of_Engineering" title="Swanson School of Engineering">Swanson School of Engineering</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_College_of_General_Studies" title="University of Pittsburgh College of General Studies">College of General Studies</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Health_and_Rehabilitation_Sciences" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences">School of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Honors_College" title="University of Pittsburgh Honors College">University Honors College</a></li> 
         </ul> </td> 
        <td style="width:40px;"></td> 
        <td> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Information_Sciences" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Information Sciences">School of Information Sciences</a></li>
