     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a> has ranked Pitt, along with only six other schools, in the top tier of U.S. public research universities and in the 6th&nbsp;tier (or top&nbsp;25) among all universities according to its 2009 annual report.<sup id="cite_ref-TheCenterRankings_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheCenterRankings-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked Pitt 19th in comparison to other <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public universities</a> in the United States and 58th among all national universities.<sup id="cite_ref-usnews2010public_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usnews2010public-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, <i>U.S. News</i> ranked Pitt 45th on the dimension of &quot;best value&quot; among all national universities,<sup id="cite_ref-USNewsBV_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNewsBV-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Princeton Review</i> placed Pitt among its &quot;Best Value Public Colleges&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-PRbestvalue_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRbestvalue-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> rated Pitt the best value in Pennsylvania and eighth best nationally for out-of-state students among public universities in their 2011 rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-KiplingerBV_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KiplingerBV-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In worldwide evaluations of universities, <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> ranked Pitt 37th in its &quot;The Top 100 Global Universities.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-The_Complete_List:_The_Top_100_Global_Universities_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Complete_List:_The_Top_100_Global_Universities-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt ranked 50th worldwide (and 37th in the U.S.) in the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Jiao_Tong_University" title="Shanghai Jiao Tong University">Shanghai Jiao Tong University's</a> <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt ranked 116th in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-QS_World_University_Rankings_2010_Results_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS_World_University_Rankings_2010_Results-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> coming 39th in the United States, and attaining 99th for Arts &amp; Humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt ranks 24th of all universities in the world for the impact and performance of its scientific public publications according to the Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities produced by the <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT).<sup id="cite_ref-HEEACT_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEEACT-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt ranks as the 26th best higher education research institution worldwide according to <a href="/wiki/SCImago" title="SCImago" class="mw-redirect">SCImago</a> Institutions Rankings' 2009 World Report.<sup id="cite_ref-SCImago_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCImago-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Other world rankings include 29th in the world in the latest ranking by the Research Center for Chinese Science Evaluation at <a href="/wiki/Wuhan_University" title="Wuhan University">Wuhan University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wuhan_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wuhan-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> 37th in the world in the latest <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics</a> rankings,<sup id="cite_ref-Webometrics_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Webometrics-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> and 42nd in the world according to both the 2006 G-Factor International University Ranking<sup id="cite_ref-G-Factor_International_University_Ranking_2006:_Top_300_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G-Factor_International_University_Ranking_2006:_Top_300-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a>-based 2009 Global University Ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-GUR_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GUR-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition to its academic rankings, Pitt has also been recognized for its positive campus atmosphere, with <a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a> rating Pitt as having the 8th happiest student body and the 11th best quality of life in the nation in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Mucha_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mucha-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Commons_Room_(Cathedral_of_Learning)_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Commons_Room_%28Cathedral_of_Learning%29_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg/170px-Commons_Room_%28Cathedral_of_Learning%29_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Commons_Room_%28Cathedral_of_Learning%29_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg/255px-Commons_Room_%28Cathedral_of_Learning%29_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Commons_Room_%28Cathedral_of_Learning%29_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg/340px-Commons_Room_%28Cathedral_of_Learning%29_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Commons_Room_(Cathedral_of_Learning)_-_Pitt_-_IMG_0573.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 52ft (16 m), half acre (2,000 m&sup2;) 
        <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning#Commons_Room" title="Cathedral of Learning">Commons Room</a> of the Cathedral of Learning serves as a major study and event space for the university and its students
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Many of university's individual schools, departments, and programs are highly regarded in their particular field as evidenced by the number of Pitt programs that were ranked in the latest <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council_rankings" title="United States National Research Council rankings">National Research Council rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_Rankings_in_Each_of_41_Areas_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_Rankings_in_Each_of_41_Areas-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Particularly well regarded programs include Pitt's Department of Philosophy, which has long been renowned in the U.S. and worldwide, and is especially strong in the areas of mathematical and philosophical logic, metaphysics, history and philosophy of science, philosophy of language, philosophy of mathematics, philosophy of mind and psychology, and semantics.<sup id="cite_ref-Welcome_to_the_2006.E2.80.932008_Philosophical_Gourmet_Report_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welcome_to_the_2006.E2.80.932008_Philosophical_Gourmet_Report-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Philosophy_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philosophy-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Pittsburgh Schools of the Health Sciences, including <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine">Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Dental_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Dental Medicine">Dental</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Nursing" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Nursing">Nursing</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Pharmacy">Pharmacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Graduate_School_of_Public_Health" title="University of Pittsburgh Graduate School of Public Health">Public Health</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Health_and_Rehabilitation_Sciences" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Health and Rehabilitation Sciences">Rehabilition</a> are also all highly ranked and regarded in their respective fields.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_ranks_graduate_programs_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_ranks_graduate_programs-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a>, is consistently honored as one of America's top hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-UPMCrank_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPMCrank-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's <a href="/wiki/Joseph_M._Katz_School_of_Business" title="Joseph M. Katz School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Joseph M. Katz School of Business</a> MBA program is ranked first in the U.S. in &quot;Value for Money,&quot; 51st overall in the nation, and its faculty research is ranked 47th in the world by the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a> ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-Katz_School_Ranks_First_in_the_Nation_for_MBA_Value_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Katz_School_Ranks_First_in_the_Nation_for_MBA_Value-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> The Joseph Katz Graduate School consistently ranks among the top ten public business schools in the U.S. according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>.</p> 
     <p>Pitt's law school faculty has been ranked 21st in the nation based upon standard objective measures of scholarly impact.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_35_Law_Faculties_Based_on_Scholarly_Impact.2C_2007_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_35_Law_Faculties_Based_on_Scholarly_Impact.2C_2007-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Overall Pitt's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Law" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Law">Law School</a> is ranked 63rd by The Law School 100,<sup id="cite_ref-Law_School_100_--_Ranking_the_Best_Law_Schools_in_the_United_States_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_School_100_--_Ranking_the_Best_Law_Schools_in_the_United_States-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> is listed among the nation's top law schools by The Princeton Review,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Princeton_Review:_University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Law_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Princeton_Review:_University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Law-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> and was ranked 91st by <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a> in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_USNWR_Law_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_USNWR_Law-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_School_Rankings_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_School_Rankings-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> down from a peak ranking of 48th in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-PRELAW_HANDBOOK_-_Law_School_Rankings:_2000-present_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRELAW_HANDBOOK_-_Law_School_Rankings:_2000-present-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt is home to the Gertrude E. and John M. Petersen Institute of <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">NanoScience</a> and Engineering, which was ranked second in the nation in 2006 for microscale and nanoscale research by the leading global trade publication, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Small_Times&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Small Times (page does not exist)">Small Times</a></i>. Pitt also has a recognized program in <a href="/wiki/Radio-frequency_identification" title="Radio-frequency identification">Radio-frequency identification</a> device (RFID) technology, with its research program rated among the top three in the world along with MIT and the University of Cambridge in England.<sup id="cite_ref-RFID_Lowdown_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFID_Lowdown-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scholars">Scholars</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Scholars">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Pitt students have regularly won national and international scholarships and fellowship awards, including four <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholarships</a> since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-pitt4_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitt4-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, in addition to the three national military academies, Pitt was one of only nine universities, and the only public university, to claim both Rhodes and Marshall Scholars. Since 1995, Pitt undergraduates have also won six <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Scholarship" title="Marshall Scholarship">Marshall Scholarships</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Scholar_winners_2013_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scholar_winners_2013-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> five <a href="/wiki/Truman_Scholarships" title="Truman Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">Truman Scholarships</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_grad_named_2010_Rhodes_Scholar_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_grad_named_2010_Rhodes_Scholar-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> seven <a href="/wiki/Morris_K._Udall_Foundation" title="Morris K. Udall Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Udall Scholarships</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Churchill_Scholarship" title="Churchill Scholarship">Churchill Scholarship</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Gates_Cambridge_Scholarship" title="Gates Cambridge Scholarship" class="mw-redirect">Gates Cambridge Scholarship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-white_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-white-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> 41&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Barry_M._Goldwater_Scholarship" title="Barry M. Goldwater Scholarship">Goldwater Scholarships</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Neuroscience_Student_From_Pennsylvania_Awarded_Goldwater_Scholarship_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Neuroscience_Student_From_Pennsylvania_Awarded_Goldwater_Scholarship-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> 23 <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Education_Program" title="National Security Education Program">Boren Scholarships</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Four_Pitt_Honors_College_Students_Receive_2010_David_L._Boren_Awards_for_International_Study_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Four_Pitt_Honors_College_Students_Receive_2010_David_L._Boren_Awards_for_International_Study-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> and three Mellon Humanities Fellowships.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_students_win_Truman.2C_Goldwater_scholarships_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_students_win_Truman.2C_Goldwater_scholarships-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_students_win_Goldwater.2C_Udall_scholarships_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_students_win_Goldwater.2C_Udall_scholarships-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt is also a leading producer of <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Program" title="Fulbright Program">Fulbright</a> scholars, placing in the top 20 of all universities in the number of student scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt alumni have won awards such as the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, the Nobel Prize in medicine, the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> for fiction, the <a href="/wiki/Shaw_Prize" title="Shaw Prize">Shaw Prize</a> in medicine, the Albany Prize in medicine, the <a href="/wiki/John_Fritz_Medal" title="John Fritz Medal">Fritz Medal</a> in engineering, the <a href="/wiki/Templeton_Prize" title="Templeton Prize">Templeton Prize</a>, and the Grainger Challenge Prize for sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-chancellor-2006_74-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chancellor-2006-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-armanlos_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-armanlos-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg/170px-ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg/255px-ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg/340px-ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ClassonHeinzChapelsteps.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A class meets outside on the steps of 
        <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Chapel</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Pitt, one of 62 elected members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, had $899&nbsp;million in research and development expenditures in 2011, ranking 10th among all universities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-NSFResearchBrief2011_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSFResearchBrief2011-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Of that amount, $663&nbsp;million was received from federal sources, the fifth largest amount of federal research sponsorship among universities and the third most among public universities.<sup id="cite_ref-NSFResearchBrief2011_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSFResearchBrief2011-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt ranked in the top 25 of all universities in the world for the impact and performance of its scientific public publications, including in the top ten for clinical medicine, according to the Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities produced by the Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-HEEACT_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEEACT-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt is also ranked 29th in the world based on Essential Science Indicators according to the Research Center for Chinese Science Evaluation of <a href="/wiki/Wuhan_University" title="Wuhan University">Wuhan University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wuhan_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wuhan-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt places much emphasis on undergraduate research and has integrated such research experience as a key component of its undergraduate experience.<sup id="cite_ref-undergrad-research_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undergrad-research-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt is a major center of biomedical research; in FY 2008, it ranked fifth in the nation in competitive peer-reviewed <a href="/wiki/NIH" title="NIH" class="mw-redirect">NIH</a> funding allocations,<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Chancellor_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Chancellor-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a> ranked 13th among hospitals nationwide by <i>USNews</i> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-UT_UPMC_HonorRoll_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UT_UPMC_HonorRoll-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Pitt neighbors the campus of <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> (CMU), and in some cases, buildings of the two universities are intermingled. This helps to facilitate a myriad of academic and research collaborations between the two schools,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> including such projects as the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Supercomputing_Center" title="Pittsburgh Supercomputing Center">Pittsburgh Supercomputing Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Life_Sciences_Greenhouse" title="Pittsburgh Life Sciences Greenhouse">Pittsburgh Life Sciences Greenhouse</a>, the Immune Modeling Center, the Center for the Neural Basis of Cognition, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Cancer_Institute" title="University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute">University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute</a>, as well as the National Science Foundation-supported Pittsburgh Science of Learning Center.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> Further, the universities also offer multiple dual and joint degree programs such as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Medicine#MD.2FPhD_Program" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine">Medical Scientist Training Program</a>, the Molecular Biophysics and Structural Biology Graduate Program, and the Law and Business Administration program. Some professors hold joint professorships between the two schools, and students at each university may take classes at the other (with appropriate approvals).<sup id="cite_ref-PCHE_Cross_Registration_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PCHE_Cross_Registration-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt students and faculty also have access to the CMU library system, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Library_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh</a>, through the Oakland Library Consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> The two universities also co-host academic conferences, such as the 2012 Second Language Research Forum.<sup id="cite_ref-SLRF_2012_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SLRF_2012-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Hail_to_Pitt" title="Hail to Pitt">Hail to Pitt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pitt_Victory_Song" title="Pitt Victory Song">Pitt Victory Song</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Alma_Mater" title="University of Pittsburgh Alma Mater">University of Pittsburgh Alma Mater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football#Traditions" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">Pitt football traditions</a></i>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <p><b>Annual Bonfire and Pep Rally</b> hosted by the Pitt Program Council is held prior to or during some football games. Held on the lawn of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, it often involves the band, cheerleaders, football team, visiting dignitaries, and giveaways.<sup id="cite_ref-Turning_up_the_heat_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turning_up_the_heat-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_traditions_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_traditions-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg/220px-PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg/330px-PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg/440px-PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:PittProgramCouncilFallFest2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A concert during Fall Fest 2008
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><b>Bigelow Bash</b> is a spring festival held by the Pitt Program Council between the <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">William Pitt Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, involving a range of activities, novelties, and bands.<sup id="cite_ref-Bigelow_Bash_features_Queens_of_the_Stone_Age_and_a_friendly_monkey_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bigelow_Bash_features_Queens_of_the_Stone_Age_and_a_friendly_monkey-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>E-Week</b> is a spring celebration organized by the Engineer Student Council for a week-long, fun-filled series of activities and competitions to demonstrate engineering skills and foster a spirit of camaraderie. Activities include games such as Monopoly, Ingenuity, Jeopardy, Assassins, and include a talent show, relay race, mini-Olympics, and blood drive. The festivities reach climax with a parade on Friday, a soapbox derby on Saturday, and the &quot;e-ball finale&quot; on Saturday evening. Each year, a unique theme is chosen. Each engineering department competes against the others, while some smaller departments join forces.<sup id="cite_ref-E-Week.27s_50th_Anniversary_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E-Week.27s_50th_Anniversary-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt.27s_School_of_Engineering_Holds_50th_Annual_E-Week_March_18.E2.80.9326:_Pittopoly.2C_Duct_Tape_Challenge.2C_and_Soap_Box_Derby_part_of_this_year.27s_festivities_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt.27s_School_of_Engineering_Holds_50th_Annual_E-Week_March_18.E2.80.9326:_Pittopoly.2C_Duct_Tape_Challenge.2C_and_Soap_Box_Derby_part_of_this_year.27s_festivities-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Fall Fest</b> is an annual fall festival held by the Pitt Program Council between the <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">William Pitt Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>, also involving a range of activities, novelties, and bands.<sup id="cite_ref-Students_celebrate_Fall_Fest_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Students_celebrate_Fall_Fest-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Football Tunnel</b> is a tradition where student organizations, carrying <a href="/wiki/Heraldic_flag" title="Heraldic flag">standards</a>, form a tunnel for the football players to run through as they enter the football field from the locker room. Originally, this long standing tradition involved only Pitt <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities and sororities</a>. The tradition was briefly lost following the 1999 season when Pitt's football program transitioned from playing in <a href="/wiki/Pitt_Stadium" title="Pitt Stadium">Pitt Stadium</a> to <a href="/wiki/Three_Rivers_Stadium" title="Three Rivers Stadium">Three Rivers Stadium</a> in 2000 followed by <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a> in 2001. The tradition was resurrected beginning with the 2008 football season.<sup id="cite_ref-cstv5_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cstv5-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Forbes Field Home Plate Slide</b> is a tradition for good luck on midterm and finals in which students slide into or step on a former home plate from <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Field" title="Forbes Field">Forbes Field</a>, where the Pittsburgh Pirates played for many seasons. The plate is on display inside <a href="/wiki/Wesley_W._Posvar_Hall" title="Wesley W. Posvar Hall">Posvar Hall</a> near its original location.<sup id="cite_ref-Campus_tour_map_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campus_tour_map-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-.27.27University_of_Pittsburgh.27.27_.28.27.27Off_the_Record.27.27.29_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.27.27University_of_Pittsburgh.27.27_.28.27.27Off_the_Record.27.27.29-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh6_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh6-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wojcichowski_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wojcichowski-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Greek Week</b> Greek Week is a yearlong initiative for the Greek organizations on campus to raise money for different charitable organizations through different events. The two biggest events each year are the Pitt Dance Marathon and Greek Sing. The Pitt Greeks have signed a contract with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Cancer_Institute" title="University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute">University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute</a> to raise $500,000 over the next five years. Yearlong fundraising activities are also held to support other charitable organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Ronald_McDonald_House" title="Ronald McDonald House" class="mw-redirect">Ronald McDonald House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Make_a_Wish_Foundation" title="Make a Wish Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Make a Wish Foundation</a>, and the Pittsburgh Food Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-Greekweek_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greekweek-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Homecoming</b>, as in other universities, revolves around one home football game each year. Pitt's homecoming involves activities hosted by the Pitt Program Council highlighted by fireworks and a laser-light display between the <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">William Pitt Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> This is followed by Casino Night in the union, the football game, and a homecoming cruise on a <a href="/wiki/Gateway_Clipper_Fleet" title="Gateway Clipper Fleet">Gateway Clipper Party Liner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Homecoming_2007_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Homecoming_2007-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Homecoming_events_include_fireworks.2C_lasers_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Homecoming_events_include_fireworks.2C_lasers-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt.27s_homecoming_history_long.2C_filled_with_memories_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt.27s_homecoming_history_long.2C_filled_with_memories-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Honors Convocation</b> is a ceremony whose modern incarnation was begun in 1977, but whose roots date to the 1930s' Scholar's Day and Tap Day.<sup id="cite_ref-Documenting_Pitt:_Honors_Convocation_Programs_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Documenting_Pitt:_Honors_Convocation_Programs-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> The Honors Convocation is typically held in late winter to present awards and recognition for academic and service achievements of the students, faculty, alumni, and staff throughout the schools and departments of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-Honors_Convocation_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honors_Convocation-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg/170px-HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg/255px-HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg/340px-HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:HeinzChapelfromBalcony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Interior of 
        <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Memorial Chapel</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><b>Lantern Night</b> is an annual ceremony, initiated in 1921 one of the University’s longest standing traditions. It is a formal induction for freshman women to university life and unites them as they begin their education at Pitt. Traditionally held on the evening before the first day of classes, the ceremony today takes place in <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Chapel</a>. Part of the Lantern Night tradition is for a distinguished alumna to give the freshman address, while other distinguished alumnae are flame bearers who light the lanterns given to each freshman woman as a keepsake.<sup id="cite_ref-Rites_of_Passage_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rites_of_Passage-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lanternpanther_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lanternpanther-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Omicron Delta Kappa Walk</b> is a stone walkway between the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Memorial Chapel</a> that contains the engraved names of Pitt's <a href="/wiki/Omicron_Delta_Kappa" title="Omicron Delta Kappa">Omicron Delta Kappa</a> Senior of the Year award winners. The walk is the only one of its kind in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Honors_College_Senior_Greg_Heller-LaBelle_Named_2006_Omicron_Delta_Kappa_Senior_of_the_Year_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Honors_College_Senior_Greg_Heller-LaBelle_Named_2006_Omicron_Delta_Kappa_Senior_of_the_Year-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Panther Sendoff</b> is an annual free reception typically held in <a href="/wiki/Alumni_Hall_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Alumni Hall (University of Pittsburgh)">Alumni Hall</a> to congratulate each year's graduating class and wish them well.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_Traditions_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_Traditions-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Rubbing the Panther Nose</b> is as another good luck tradition in which students rub the nose of the <a href="/wiki/Panthers_of_Pittsburgh#Millennium_Panther" title="Panthers of Pittsburgh">Millennium Panther</a> outside the <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Union" title="William Pitt Union">William Pitt Union</a> prior to exams.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Alumn_Association:_Traditions:_When_You_Wish_Upon_a_Panther_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Alumn_Association:_Traditions:_When_You_Wish_Upon_a_Panther-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> This tradition has further grown into one that is used by the wider university community when seeking general good fortune and was featured in a national television advertisement for the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Tucson" title="Hyundai Tucson">Hyundai Tucson</a> automobile.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>University of Pittsburgh Annual Jazz Seminar and Concert</b> is a fall lecture and concert series founded by <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Davis_(saxophonist)" title="Nathan Davis (saxophonist)">Dr. Nathan Davis</a>, professor in the Music Department, and University officials in 1970. Renowned jazz musicians, critics, and historians lead seminar sessions for students and others in the local jazz community. These sessions are free and open to the public and deal with topics ranging from entering the music business to practice techniques, composing, arranging, and individual instrument mastery. Previous musicians who have attending include <a href="/wiki/Dizzy_Gillespie" title="Dizzy Gillespie">Dizzy Gillespie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Clarke" title="Kenny Clarke">Kenny Clarke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Rollins" title="Sonny Rollins">Sonny Rollins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dexter_Gordon" title="Dexter Gordon">Dexter Gordon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Max_Roach" title="Max Roach">Max Roach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Jazz_Seminar_.26_Concert_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Jazz_Seminar_.26_Concert-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:PittVarsityWalk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/PittVarsityWalk.jpg/250px-PittVarsityWalk.jpg" width="250" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/PittVarsityWalk.jpg/375px-PittVarsityWalk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/PittVarsityWalk.jpg/500px-PittVarsityWalk.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:PittVarsityWalk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Varsity Walk
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><b>Varsity Walk</b> is a walkway between the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Memorial_Chapel" title="Heinz Memorial Chapel">Heinz Memorial Chapel</a> on which is carved the names of former Pitt athletes (each year since 1950) who have promoted the University through their athletic (Panther Award) or academic (Blue-Gold Award) achievements.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Varsity_Walk_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Varsity_Walk-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Victory Lights</b> is a tradition where golden flood lights illuminate the top of the Cathedral of Learning after every football victory.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_traditions_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_traditions-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pittnews_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pittnews-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Secrets_of_the_Cathedral:_Starting_at_the_top_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Secrets_of_the_Cathedral:_Starting_at_the_top-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pitt_Arts">Pitt Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Pitt Arts">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><b>Pitt Arts</b> is a program founded by the University in 1997 to encourage students to explore and connect to the art and cultural opportunities of the City of Pittsburgh via three programs. <i>Art Encounters</i> provides trips to arts events for undergrads that include free tickets, transportation, a catered reception, and encounters with international artists and thinkers. <i>Free Visits</i> grants undergrad and grad students free admission using their Pitt IDs to the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Museum of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Museum of Natural History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_History_Center" title="Heinz History Center">Senator John Heinz History Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phipps_Conservatory_%26_Botanical_Gardens" title="Phipps Conservatory &amp; Botanical Gardens">Phipps Conservatory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mattress_Factory" title="Mattress Factory">Mattress Factory</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">Andy Warhol Museum</a>. <i>Cheap Seats</i> is a program that everyone at Pitt can use to take advantage of deeply-discounted tickets to the most sought-after arts events in the area, including the Pittsburgh <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Ballet_Theatre" title="Pittsburgh Ballet Theatre">ballet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Opera" title="Pittsburgh Opera">opera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Pittsburgh Symphony Orchestra">symphony</a>, theater, concerts, and other <a href="/wiki/Cultural_District,_Pittsburgh" title="Cultural District, Pittsburgh">cultural district</a> activities.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_arts_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_arts-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PITT_ARTS_Reaches_More_Than_32.2C000_Participants_This_Year_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PITT_ARTS_Reaches_More_Than_32.2C000_Participants_This_Year-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_theater">Student theater</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Student theater">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:StephenfosterDoors.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/StephenfosterDoors.jpg/220px-StephenfosterDoors.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/StephenfosterDoors.jpg/330px-StephenfosterDoors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/StephenfosterDoors.jpg/440px-StephenfosterDoors.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:StephenfosterDoors.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Pitt's 
        <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Foster_Memorial" title="Stephen Foster Memorial">Stephen Foster Memorial</a> contains two theaters.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Repertory_Theatre" title="University of Pittsburgh Repertory Theatre">University of Pittsburgh Repertory Theatre</a></b>, or Pitt Rep, is the production company of the Department of Theatre Arts which puts public student performances of classic masterpieces, contemporary productions, and student-directed labs. It also runs the Shakespeare-in-the-Schools which tours classic theater for K-12 students throughout the Pittsburgh area.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Department_of_Theatre_Arts_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Department_of_Theatre_Arts-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Friday_Nite_Improvs" title="Friday Nite Improvs">Friday Nite Improvs</a></b>, Pittsburgh's longest-running theatre show, was started in 1989 by graduate theatre students. It takes place weekly inside the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>'s studio theatre.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Kuntu_Repertory_Theatre" title="Kuntu Repertory Theatre">Kuntu Repertory Theatre</a></b>, founded in 1974, is the second-oldest African American performing arts organization affiliated with a major research university. It promotes and encourages participation in theater arts centered on the African heritage and experience.<sup id="cite_ref-Kuntu_Repertory_Theatre_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuntu_Repertory_Theatre-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The <b>Redeye Theatre Project</b> is a festival of one-act plays cast, written, and rehearsed in 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-Redeye_Theatre_Project_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Redeye_Theatre_Project-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b>Pitt Musical Theater Club</b> provides undergraduates the opportunity to perform in student directed variety shows and musicals. The club was founded in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Musical_Theater_Club_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Musical_Theater_Club-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_music">Student music</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Student music">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MusicbuildPitt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/MusicbuildPitt.jpg/170px-MusicbuildPitt.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/MusicbuildPitt.jpg/255px-MusicbuildPitt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/MusicbuildPitt.jpg/340px-MusicbuildPitt.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MusicbuildPitt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Music_Building_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Music Building (University of Pittsburgh)">Music Building</a> once served as home to the original studio for 
        <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Rogers%27_Neighborhood" title="Mr. Rogers' Neighborhood" class="mw-redirect">Mr. Rogers' Neighborhood</a></i>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Pitt Men's Glee Club</b>, founded in 1890, is the oldest extracurricular club on campus. The internationally showcased<sup id="cite_ref-PMGC_in_Bologna-_Beatus_Vir_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMGC_in_Bologna-_Beatus_Vir-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> club includes both undergraduate and graduate students from throughout the University. Traditionally, the Glee Club has sung for a variety of campus-wide and community functions, including graduations, receptions, alumni gatherings, sporting events, and chancellor's events. The Glee Club has also participated in national Collegiate Men's Choir festivals and international music festivals aside from seasonal concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Men.27s_Glee_Club_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Men.27s_Glee_Club-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Heinz_Chapel_Choir" title="Heinz Chapel Choir">Heinz Chapel Choir</a></b> is an accomplished and internationally-known<sup id="cite_ref-Heinz_Chapel_choir_program_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinz_Chapel_choir_program-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>a cappella</i> choir consisting entirely of Pitt students that has been performing for over 70 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinz_Chapel_Choir_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinz_Chapel_Choir-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>University of Pittsburgh Women's Choral Ensemble</b>, founded in 1927, is open to all women of the University including undergraduates, graduate students, and staff. The ensemble leads the traditional lamplighter processional each fall and performs repertory ranging from traditional sacred and secular classics to international folk songs, popular music, and show tunes.<sup id="cite_ref-Department_of_Music:_Women.27s_Choral_Ensemble_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Department_of_Music:_Women.27s_Choral_Ensemble-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>University of Pittsburgh Orchestra</b> performs several concerts and consists of music students, students from the University at large, faculty, staff, and members of the metropolitan community. The orchestra performs not only works of the standard art music literature, but also new works of student composers.<sup id="cite_ref-Department_of_Music:_The_University_Orchestra_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Department_of_Music:_The_University_Orchestra-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Pitt Jazz Ensemble</b>, founded in 1969, has been recognized internationally<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as one of the best collegiate jazz groups.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Under the direction of <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Davis_(saxophonist)" title="Nathan Davis (saxophonist)">Dr. Davis</a>, the ensemble has performed around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Pittsburgh_Jazz_Ensemble_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pittsburgh_Jazz_Ensemble-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Pitt African Music and Dance Ensemble</b>, founded in 1983 by a Ghanaian ethnomusicologist Dr. Willie O. Anku, specializes in music and dances from Africa. Under the direction of J. S. Kofi Gbolonyo, it presents a range of African artistic expressions including music, dance, drama and visual arts.<sup id="cite_ref-Department_of_Music:_African_Music_and_dance_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Department_of_Music:_African_Music_and_dance-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Pitt_Band" title="Pitt Band" class="mw-redirect">Pitt Band</a></b>, founded in 1911, is the varsity marching band of the University of Pittsburgh and performs at various athletic and other University events.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Pitt Pendulums</b>, founded in 1996, is a co-ed a cappella group. The group performs at a variety of on- and off- campus events, including tours of the United States and Canada. The Pendulums are annual competitors in the <a href="/wiki/International_Championship_of_Collegiate_A_Cappella" title="International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella">International Championship of Collegiate A Cappella</a><sup id="cite_ref-The_Pittsburgh_Pendulums:_History_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Pittsburgh_Pendulums:_History-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> and were most recently featured on <a href="/wiki/WQED_(TV)" title="WQED (TV)">WQED</a>'s <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.wqed.org/ondemand/onq.php?cat=3&amp;id=488">OnQ</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WQED_OnQ_OnDemand:_The_Pitt_Pendulums_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WQED_OnQ_OnDemand:_The_Pitt_Pendulums-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Sounds of Pleasure</b>, founded in 1997, is an all-female a cappella group.<sup id="cite_ref-Sounds_of_Pleasure_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sounds_of_Pleasure-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>VoKols</b>, founded in 2006, is a co-ed a cappella group that sings a combination of American and Hebrew pop music.<sup id="cite_ref-Hillel_JUC-_VoKols:_History_of_the_VoKols_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillel_JUC-_VoKols:_History_of_the_VoKols-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b>Carpathian Ensemble</b>, founded within the Department of music in 2008, the ensemble performs <a href="/wiki/Romani_music" title="Romani music">Gypsy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Klezmer" title="Klezmer">Klezmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Armenia" title="Music of Armenia">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Moldova" title="Music of Moldova">Moldavian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Ukraine" title="Music of Ukraine">Ukrainian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Music of the Republic of Macedonia">Macedonian</a> music.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG/170px-Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG/255px-Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG/340px-Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Wesley_Wentz_Posvar_Hall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Wesley_W._Posvar_Hall" title="Wesley W. Posvar Hall">Wesley W. Posvar Hall</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/WPTS-FM" title="WPTS-FM">WPTS-FM</a></b> is a non-commercial radio station owned by the University of Pittsburgh, and offers a mix of student-run programming. The station operates at 92.1 <a href="/wiki/Megahertz" title="Megahertz" class="mw-redirect">MHz</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Effective_radiated_power" title="Effective radiated power">ERP</a> of 16 watts, and is licensed to Pittsburgh.</li> 
      <li><i><b><a href="/wiki/JURIST" title="JURIST">JURIST</a></b></i> is the world's only law-school-based, comprehensive, legal news and research service staffed by a mostly-volunteer team of part-time law student reporters, editors and Web developers. It is led by law professor Bernard Hibbitts at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Law" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Law">University of Pittsburgh School of Law</a>.</li> 
      <li><i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Pitt_News" title="The Pitt News">The Pitt News</a></b></i> is an independent, student-written, and student-managed newspaper for the University's Oakland (main) campus. Founded in 1908, it is now published Monday through Friday during the school year and Wednesdays during the summer. It circulates 14,000 copies for each issue published.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/UPTV_(University_of_Pittsburgh_Television)" title="UPTV (University of Pittsburgh Television)">UPTV (University of Pittsburgh Television)</a></b> is a student-managed, student-produced, closed-circuit television station. As of June 2006, only students living in campus residence halls or university operated-housing can view programming.</li> 
      <li><i><b><a href="/wiki/Three_Rivers_Review" title="Three Rivers Review">Three Rivers Review</a></b></i> and <i><b>Collision</b></i> are two undergraduate, bi-annual, literary journals publishing both poetry and prose.</li> 
      <li><i><b><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh_Undergraduate_Review&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pittsburgh Undergraduate Review (page does not exist)">The Pittsburgh Undergraduate Review</a></b></i> is a multidisciplinary journal showcasing undergraduate research.</li> 
      <li><i><b>Pitt Political Review</b></i> is a student-created, student-written publication of the University Honors College. PPR, as it is called, provides a venue for serious discussion of politics and policy issues in a nonpartisan way.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Political_Review_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Political_Review-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i><b><a href="/wiki/The_Original_Magazine" title="The Original Magazine">The Original Magazine</a></b></i> is a nonprofit, semiannual arts and culture publication based at, and partially funded by, the University of Pittsburgh, that aims to both bring and publicize accessible art and creative writing to Pittsburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Original_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Original-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:AlumniHallatPitt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/AlumniHallatPitt.jpg/220px-AlumniHallatPitt.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/AlumniHallatPitt.jpg/330px-AlumniHallatPitt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/AlumniHallatPitt.jpg/440px-AlumniHallatPitt.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:AlumniHallatPitt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Alumni_Hall_(University_of_Pittsburgh)" title="Alumni Hall (University of Pittsburgh)">Alumni Hall</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>There are over 350 student clubs and organizations at the University of Pittsburgh all sizes and covering all manner of interests.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Freshman_Prospectus_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Freshman_Prospectus-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the larger ones include the following, presented in alphabetical order.</p> 
     <p><b>Black Action Society</b> is the recognized student organization for promoting the cultural, educational, political, and social needs of black students at the university. It comprises nine committees including the publication of the student-run publication <i>BlackLine</i> as well as community outreach, political action, and programing.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> In the past the BAS has hosted lectures by such figures as <a href="/wiki/Cornel_West" title="Cornel West">Cornel West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spike_Lee" title="Spike Lee">Spike Lee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carol_Mosley-Braun" title="Carol Mosley-Braun" class="mw-redirect">Carol Mosley-Braun</a>.</p> 
     <p><b>Blue and Gold Society</b>, founded in 1991, is a group of undergraduate student leaders chosen as liaisons between the student community and the Pitt Alumni Association.<sup id="cite_ref-Blue_and_Gold_Society_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blue_and_Gold_Society-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <b>Chinese American Students Association (CASA)</b> strives to provide a community on campus where students that share the same interests in both Chinese and Chinese American culture may congregate and share this interest through events and activities such as, the annual Chinese New Years Festival and the annual Mid-Autumn Festival.</p> 
     <p><b>Graduate and Professional Student Government (GPSG)</b> is the student government that represents the interests of all graduate and professional student at the University of Pittsburgh and serves as the umbrella organization for all of the graduate/professional school student governments. GPSG's mission is to ensure that the concerns of these students are heard and also provides services and programs such travel grants, legal and financial consulting, and social functions.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Graduate_and_Professional_Student_Association_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Graduate_and_Professional_Student_Association-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Hillel: Jewish Student Union (JSU)</b>, is a pluralistic Jewish community that serves all Pitt undergraduates. Programs take place on campus and at the Hillel Jewish University Center at 4607 Forbes Avenue. Events include holiday, interfaith, Jewish education, social action, arts and cultural programming as well as no-fee weekly Shabbat services and dinner every Friday night.<sup id="cite_ref-Hillel:_Jewish_Student_Union_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillel:_Jewish_Student_Union-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:TowersfromPosvar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/TowersfromPosvar.jpg/170px-TowersfromPosvar.jpg" width="170" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/TowersfromPosvar.jpg/255px-TowersfromPosvar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/TowersfromPosvar.jpg/340px-TowersfromPosvar.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:TowersfromPosvar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_Towers" title="Litchfield Towers">Litchfield Towers</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/David_Lawrence_Hall" title="David Lawrence Hall">David Lawrence Hall</a> (right)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><b>Student Government Board (SGB)</b> is the governing body that provides undergraduate students with representation to the university administration, presenting their needs, interests, and concerns. Another important aspect of the SGB is allocation of the student activities fee, which provides money to over 350 student organizations at the University of Pittsburgh. The SGB also has ten standing committees who address various aspects of campus life, including diversity, freshman involvement, and governmental relations.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Student_Government_Board_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Student_Government_Board-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b><a href="/wiki/Oakland_Zoo_(cheering_section)" title="Oakland Zoo (cheering section)">Oakland Zoo</a></b> is the student athletic cheering section, and is an officially recognized student club by the University of Pittsburgh. At over 2,000 members, it is the largest such group at the University. The group helps participate with the Athletic Department and Pitt Student Government Board in setting student ticket policy as well as organizing special student events.<sup id="cite_ref-Oakland_Zoo_Club_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oakland_Zoo_Club-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Pitt Pathfinders</b> is a student-run organization that hosts campus tours, assists prospective students in making well-informed college-related decisions, and promotes Pitt pride.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Pathfinders_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Pathfinders-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Pitt Program Council</b> is the all-campus programming organization at the university. Comprising eight student committees, a variety of programs and festivities are planned and sponsored including Fall Fest, Bigelow Bash, Homecoming Laser and Fireworks Show, as well as trips to New York City, Cedar Point, Spring break in Panama City Beach, FL. Other activities include art gallery exhibits, films, horseback riding, sports tournaments, lectures, fitness and dance classes, and Black and White Ball.<sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Program_Council_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Program_Council-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Quo Vadis</b> is a student organization that conducts guided tours and interpretations of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning's</a> 29 <a href="/wiki/Nationality_Rooms" title="Nationality Rooms">Nationality Rooms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Quo_Vadis_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quo_Vadis-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Rainbow Alliance</b> is a student advocacy group for Gay, Lesbian, Bisexual, Transgender, Queer, and Allied students. Among other activities, Pitt Rainbow Alliance holds an Annual Drag Show to raise money for Pittsburgh AIDS Task Force.<sup id="cite_ref-Rainbow_Alliance_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rainbow_Alliance-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b>Telefact</b> is an informational telephone service run by students that researches and answers callers' questions. The service is free to use and can be reached at 412–624-FACT.</p> 
     <p><b>University of Pittsburgh Mock Trial</b> is a yearlong extracurricular activity open to Pitt undergraduates that provides an opportunity to learn about the practice of litigation through a series of team-based <a href="/wiki/Mock_trial" title="Mock trial">mock trial</a> competitions. Pitt Mock Trial has qualified for American Mock Trial Association post-season tournaments each of the last six years, finishing in the fifth overall place at the 2008 National Championship Tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-University_of_Pittsburgh_Mock_Trial_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Pittsburgh_Mock_Trial-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Honors_College_Mock_Trial_Team_Places_Fifth_in_American_Mock_Trial_Association_National_Competition_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Honors_College_Mock_Trial_Team_Places_Fifth_in_American_Mock_Trial_Association_National_Competition-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><b><a href="/wiki/William_Pitt_Debating_Union" title="William Pitt Debating Union">William Pitt Debating Union</a></b> is a co-curricular program and hub for a wide range of debating activities, including intercollegiate policy debate, public debate, and debate outreach. 1981 <a href="/wiki/National_Debate_Tournament" title="National Debate Tournament">National Debate Tournament</a> champions,<sup id="cite_ref-Results_from_Previous_National_Debate_Tournament.2C_1977-1986_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Results_from_Previous_National_Debate_Tournament.2C_1977-1986-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> it has qualified for the National Debate Tournament forty times<sup id="cite_ref-National_Debate_Tournament_Participating_Schools.2C_1947.E2.80.932006_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Debate_Tournament_Participating_Schools.2C_1947.E2.80.932006-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> and is one of the oldest organizations of its kind in the nation, growing from the University’s Division of Public Speaking in 1912.<sup id="cite_ref-William_Pitt_Debating_Union_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William_Pitt_Debating_Union-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg/170px-HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg/255px-HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg/340px-HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:HillmanLibUnivPitt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Hillman_Library" title="Hillman Library">Hillman Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As of 2008, the University of Pittsburgh <a href="/wiki/Greek_system" title="Greek system" class="mw-redirect">Greek system</a> raised $285,000 for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Cancer_Institute" title="University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute">University of Pittsburgh Cancer Institute</a>. The effort is part of the Pittsburgh Greek system's five-year pledge to raise $500,000 for the cancer center.<sup id="cite_ref-Greekweek_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greekweek-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
