     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">Pittsburgh Panthers</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Heinz_Field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Heinz_Field.jpg/220px-Heinz_Field.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Heinz_Field.jpg/330px-Heinz_Field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Heinz_Field.jpg/440px-Heinz_Field.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Heinz_Field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a>, home of 
        <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">Pitt football</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Pittsburgh's athletic teams, referred to as the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">Pittsburgh Panthers</a>&quot; or &quot;Pitt Panthers,&quot; include 19 university-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity</a> teams at the highest level of competitive collegiate athletics in the United States: the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division&nbsp;I</a> (NCAA Division 1 <a href="/wiki/Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="Football Bowl Subdivision" class="mw-redirect">Football Bowl Subdivision</a> (FBS) for <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">american football</a>).</p> 
     <p>Varsity men's sports sponsored by the university are <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_baseball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers baseball">baseball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_men%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers men's basketball">basketball</a>, cross country, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">football</a>, soccer, swimming and diving, indoor track and field, outdoor track and field, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_wrestling" title="Pittsburgh Panthers wrestling">wrestling</a>; while sponsored women's varsity sports include <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_women%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers women's basketball">basketball</a>, cross country, gymnastics, soccer, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_softball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers softball">softball</a>, swimming and diving, tennis, indoor track and field, outdoor track and field, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_volleyball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers volleyball" class="mw-redirect">volleyball</a>. All varsity sports teams compete as members of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">Atlantic Coast Conference</a> (ACC) since the 2013-14 season, with the exception of the gymnastics team competing in the <a href="/wiki/East_Atlantic_Gymnastics_League" title="East Atlantic Gymnastics League">East Atlantic Gymnastics League</a> (EAGL). The university also maintains membership in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_College_Athletic_Conference" title="Eastern College Athletic Conference">Eastern College Athletic Conference</a> (ECAC).</p> 
     <p>Scholastically, during 2012 calendar year, out of approximately 450 Pitt varsity student athletes, 350 had term grade point averages exceeding 3.0, including 16 that had a perfect average of 4.0, and 174 were named <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">Big East Conference</a> Academic All-Stars or placed on the all-academic Big East football team.<sup id="cite_ref-Scholar_Athletes_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scholar_Athletes-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> The Big East was Pitt's conference affiliation prior to 2013.</p> 
     <p>There are also approximate 30 additional athletic teams that compete at the non-varsity club sports level.</p> 
     <p>Pitt’s highest-profile athletic programs, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">American football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_men%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers men's basketball">men’s basketball</a>, are consistently competitive. Pitt has been regularly ranked as having one of the best combinations of football and basketball programs by multiple sports media outlets,<sup id="cite_ref-2010_Hoops_.26_Helmets_Rankings_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Hoops_.26_Helmets_Rankings-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Best_of_both:_BCS_era_combined_standings_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Best_of_both:_BCS_era_combined_standings-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/CBSSports.com" title="CBSSports.com">CBS Sports</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Flourishing_Five_No._5:_Resurgent_Pitt_football_doing_its_part_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flourishing_Five_No._5:_Resurgent_Pitt_football_doing_its_part-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN.com_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN.com-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-All-Sport_Rankings_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-All-Sport_Rankings-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the fall of 1909, the University of Pittsburgh was the first college or university to adopt the panther (<i><a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">Puma concolor</a></i>) as its mascot.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Panther_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Panther-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Popular as photo sites, there are ten representations of Panthers in and about Pitt's campus, and ten more painted fiberglass panthers placed around the campus by the Pitt Student Government. These fiberglass panther structures are given to a campus group for a year and painted by the group to reflect their interests. The oldest representations are four panthers that guard each corner of the Panther Hollow bridge. Other Oakland locations include both inside and in front of the William Pitt Union, outside the Petersen Events Center, &quot;Pitt the Panther&quot; on the carousel in Schenley Plaza, the Panther head fountain on the front of the Cathedral of Learning, and the Pitt Panther statue outside Heinz Field on Pittsburgh's North Side.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">Pittsburgh Panthers football</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Traditionally the most popular sport at the University of Pittsburgh, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">football</a> has been played at the highest levels at the University since 1890. During the more than 100 years of competitive football at Pitt, the University has helped pioneer the sport by, among other things, instituting the use of numbers on jerseys<sup id="cite_ref-Hail_to_Pitt:_A_Sports_History_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hail_to_Pitt:_A_Sports_History_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> and desegregating the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Bowl" title="Sugar Bowl">Sugar Bowl</a>. Some of college football's all-time greatest coaches and players have plied their trade at Pitt, including <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Scobey_Warner" title="Glenn Scobey Warner">Pop Warner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jock_Sutherland" title="Jock Sutherland">Jock Sutherland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Goldberg" title="Marshall Goldberg">Marshall Goldberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Schmidt" title="Joe Schmidt">Joe Schmidt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Ditka" title="Mike Ditka">Mike Ditka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Dorsett" title="Tony Dorsett">Tony Dorsett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Green_(American_football)" title="Hugh Green (American football)">Hugh Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_May" title="Mark May">Mark May</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Marino" title="Dan Marino">Dan Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Fralic" title="Bill Fralic">Bill Fralic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Martin" title="Curtis Martin">Curtis Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darrelle_Revis" title="Darrelle Revis">Darrelle Revis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russ_Grimm" title="Russ Grimm">Russ Grimm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Fitzgerald" title="Larry Fitzgerald">Larry Fitzgerald</a>. Among the top schools in terms of all-time wins, Pitt teams have claimed nine <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football#National_Championships" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">National Championships</a><sup id="cite_ref-Pitt_Athletics_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pitt_Athletics-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> and boast 86&nbsp;players that have been chosen as first-team All-Americans.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg/220px-2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg/330px-2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg/440px-2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:2009PittUConn2ndmin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_men%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers men's basketball">Pitt basketball</a> in the 
        <a href="/wiki/Petersen_Events_Center" title="Petersen Events Center">Petersen Events Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_men%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers men's basketball">Pittsburgh Panthers men's basketball</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_women%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers women's basketball">Pittsburgh Panthers women's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Pitt first sponsored varsity <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_men%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers men's basketball">men's basketball</a> in 1905 and became an early national power after winning two Helms Foundation National Championships in 1927–28 and 1929–30. Those teams, coached by the innovative and legendary <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Basketball Hall of Fame" class="mw-redirect">Naismith Hall of Fame</a> inductee <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Carlson" title="Clifford Carlson">&quot;Doc&quot; Carlson</a>, were led by National Player of the Year and Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Hyatt" title="Chuck Hyatt">Charlie Hyatt</a>. Following a <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Final Four</a> appearance in 1941, Pitt appeared in a handful of NCAA tournaments throughout the 1950s, 1960s, and 1970s, including an Elite Eight appearance in 1974 led by All-American <a href="/wiki/Billy_Knight" title="Billy Knight">Billy Knight</a>. Pitt joined the Big East Conference in 1982, and by the end of the decade had secured a pair of Big East regular season championships led by All-Americans <a href="/wiki/Charles_D._Smith" title="Charles D. Smith" class="mw-redirect">Charles Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Lane" title="Jerome Lane">Jerome Lane</a>. In the 2000s (decade), led by coach <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dixon" title="Jamie Dixon">Jamie Dixon</a>, an era of consistent national and conference competitiveness has been achieved, including reaching the number one ranking in various national polls. Since 2002, Pitt has appeared in eleven NCAA tournaments advancing to five Sweet Sixteens and an Elite Eight. During this time, prior to joining the Atlantic Coast Conference in 2013, Pitt and has won three Big East regular season championships, two Big East Tournament Championships, and has advanced to six Big East Tournament Championship games.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_women%27s_basketball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers women's basketball">Pittsburgh Panthers women's varsity basketball program</a> started during the 1914–1915 school year and lasted until 1927 before going on hiatus until 1970. Pitt's women's team has posted several NCAA, NWIT, and EAIAW tournament appearances. Led head coach <a href="/wiki/Agnus_Berenato" title="Agnus Berenato">Agnus Berenato</a>, Pitt has played in post-season tournaments each of the last five seasons, including three <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournaments</a> appearances where it advanced to the Sweet Sixteen in 2008 and 2009.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_sports">Olympic sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Olympic sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg/150px-Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg.png" width="150" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg/225px-Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg/300px-Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Panthers_Alternate_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The current Panther logo is a stylized panther head introduced in 1997 designed to suggest that it was cut by a welding torch from steel.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_baseball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers baseball">Pittsburgh Panthers baseball</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_softball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers softball">Pittsburgh Panthers softball</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_volleyball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers volleyball" class="mw-redirect">Pittsburgh Panthers volleyball</a>,&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_wrestling" title="Pittsburgh Panthers wrestling">Pittsburgh Panthers wrestling</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Pitt has had a long history of success in other intercollegiate athletic events. In <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers#Track_and_Field" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">Track and Field</a>, Pitt has produced several Olympic and NCAA champions such as 800 m Olympic gold medalist <a href="/wiki/John_Woodruff" title="John Woodruff">John Woodruff</a>, two-time 110&nbsp;m hurdle Olympic gold medalist <a href="/wiki/Roger_Kingdom" title="Roger Kingdom">Roger Kingdom</a>, and seven-time NCAA champion and 2005 World Champion <a href="/wiki/Triple_jump" title="Triple jump">triple jumper</a> <a href="/wiki/Trecia_Smith" title="Trecia Smith" class="mw-redirect">Trecia-Kaye Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cstv_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cstv-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_wrestling" title="Pittsburgh Panthers wrestling">wrestling program</a> has a rich history and is among the leaders in producing individual national champions with 16.<sup id="cite_ref-PITT_Wrestling_Media_Guide_2006.E2.80.932007_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PITT_Wrestling_Media_Guide_2006.E2.80.932007-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt's <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_volleyball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers volleyball" class="mw-redirect">women's volleyball</a> team, one of the winningest program in the nation,<sup id="cite_ref-Volleyball_Releases_2007_Schedule_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volleyball_Releases_2007_Schedule-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> won 11 conference championships while a member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference_(1979%E2%80%932013)" title="Big East Conference (1979–2013)">Big East</a>, and appeared in 11&nbsp;NCAA tournaments since the program began in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-2006_Pitt_Volleyball_Media_Guide_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2006_Pitt_Volleyball_Media_Guide-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> Pitt's <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers#Swimming_and_Diving" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">swimming and diving teams</a> have produced several Olympians and won 19 men's and nine women's Big East Championships while a member of that conference. Pitt <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers#Gymnastics" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">women's gymnastics</a> is a regular qualifier for the NCAA Northeast Regional Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-PITT_Gymnastics_Media_Guide_2007_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PITT_Gymnastics_Media_Guide_2007-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_baseball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers baseball">Baseball</a>, Pitt's oldest varsity sport, has produced several major league players and has reached the national 25 repeatedly, including in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> Other varsity sports have also found varying degrees of success and include <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers#Cross_Country" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">cross country</a>, soccer, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_softball" title="Pittsburgh Panthers softball">softball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers#Tennis" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">tennis</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Support_groups">Support groups</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Support groups">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The history-rich <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Varsity_Marching_Band" title="University of Pittsburgh Varsity Marching Band">University of Pittsburgh Varsity Marching Band</a> was founded in 1911 and performs at athletic and other events. The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers#Pitt_Cheerleaders_and_Dance_Team" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">Pitt cheerleading squad</a> has won multiple <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">cheerleading</a> national championships, including three straight from 1992–1994. The Pitt dance team also has been competitive in national competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-Spirit_Groups_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spirit_Groups-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cheer_and_Dance_Finish_in_Top_20_in_Respective_Competitions_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cheer_and_Dance_Finish_in_Top_20_in_Respective_Competitions-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_notable_University_of_Pittsburgh_people" title="List of notable University of Pittsburgh people" class="mw-redirect">List of notable University of Pittsburgh people</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heads_of_the_university">Heads of the university</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Heads of the university">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_History#Heads_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh History" class="mw-redirect">Heads of the University of Pittsburgh</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Pittsburgh has had many individuals lead it throughout its history. During the academy days, the title of Principal was worn by the head of the school. Due to fires, early records are incomplete. When Pittsburgh Academy transitioned into the Western University, the title was changed to Chancellor. This title has lasted except for a brief change during Wesley Posvar's administration when it was transiently switched to President. Samuel McCormick oversaw the name change from the Western University of Pennsylvania to the University of Pittsburgh in 1908 and is therefore listed with the chancellors of the University of Pittsburgh. Acting chancellors are also included in the list below. For more information on past heads of the University, and for photos, please see <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_History#Heads_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh History" class="mw-redirect">Pitt History: Heads of the University</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni_and_faculty">Alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Alumni and faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Alumni have won awards and prizes that include the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Arts" title="National Medal of Arts">National Medal of Arts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Perkin_Medal" title="Perkin Medal">Perkin Medal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology" title="National Medal of Technology" class="mw-redirect">National Medal of Technology</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellows_Program" title="MacArthur Fellows Program">MacArthur &quot;Genius Award&quot;</a>.<sup class="noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style_(dates_and_numbers)" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style (dates and numbers)" class="mw-redirect"><span title="This term requires quantification. (January 2013)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-chancellor-2006_74-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chancellor-2006-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-armanlos_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-armanlos-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Legacy_Gallery_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Legacy_Gallery-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Strictly_Bill_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strictly_Bill-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> The faculty and alumni have been pioneers in such fields as <a href="/wiki/John_Brashear" title="John Brashear">astronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Pierpont_Langley" title="Samuel Pierpont Langley">aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Salk" title="Jonas Salk">virology</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Wistar_Simpson" title="John Wistar Simpson">nuclear energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Spock" title="Benjamin Spock">psychology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Boyer" title="Herbert Boyer">genetics</a> in addition to being given popular titles such as the <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Fessenden" title="Reginald Fessenden">Father of Radio Broadcasting</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Zworykin" title="Vladimir Zworykin" class="mw-redirect">Father of Television</a>, the <a href="/wiki/David_I._Cleland" title="David I. Cleland">Father of Project Management</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Peter_Safar" title="Peter Safar">Father of CPR</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lauterbur" title="Paul Lauterbur">Father of the MRI</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Starzl" title="Thomas Starzl">Father of Organ Transplantation</a>.</p>

       <li id="cite_note-pittsburgh-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-pittsburgh_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This figure reflects the total number of faculty at the Pittsburgh campus only. 403 additional faculty serve the four regional campuses for a university-wide total of 5,210 faculty members.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-enrollfn-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-enrollfn_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-enrollfn_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">This enrollment figure reflects the total headcount of full-time and part-time undergraduate and graduate students attending classes at the University of Pittsburgh-Pittsburgh Campus in Fall 2010 only. An additional 6,911 full-time and part-time undergraduate students attend the university across the four regional campuses for a university-wide headcount of 35,734 total students, 25,282 of which are undergraduates.</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Pitt:_The_Story_of_the_University_of_Pittsburgh_1787.E2.80.931987_6-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Upon joining the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Commonwealth System of Higher Education">Commonwealth System of Higher Education</a> in 1966, the University of Pittsburgh legally remained a private entity and in practice, retained the administrative and academic freedom of a private institution. It sets its own standards for student admission and retention, faculty, and teaching. Its assets remain in the hands of the corporation, its employees are employed by the corporation, and its affairs are governed by an independent Board of Trustees.<sup><i>A</i></sup> In-state tuition is subsidized by the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania and the state provides approximately 11% of its operating budget.<sup><i>B</i></sup> The University of Pittsburgh is categorized as a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public university</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Foundation Classifications</a><sup><i>C</i></sup> and is typically listed as a public university in third party publications.<sup><i>D</i></sup> For simplicity, Pitt sometimes refers to itself a &quot;public university&quot;.&nbsp;:<sup><i>A</i></sup><span class="citation book">Alberts, Robert C. (1986). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://digital.library.pitt.edu/cgi-bin/t/text/pageviewer-idx?c=pittmiscpubs&amp;idno=00c50130m&amp;seq=363"><i>Pitt: The Story of the University of Pittsburgh 1787–1987</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Press" title="University of Pittsburgh Press">University of Pittsburgh Press</a>. p.&nbsp;343. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-8229-1150-7" title="Special:BookSources/0-8229-1150-7">0-8229-1150-7</a>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUniversity+of+Pittsburgh&amp;rft.au=Alberts%2C+Robert+C.&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert+C.&amp;rft.aulast=Alberts&amp;rft.btitle=Pitt%3A+The+Story+of+the+University+of+Pittsburgh+1787%E2%80%931987&amp;rft.date=1986&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fdigital.library.pitt.edu%2Fcgi-bin%2Ft%2Ftext%2Fpageviewer-idx%3Fc%3Dpittmiscpubs%26idno%3D00c50130m%26seq%3D363&amp;rft.isbn=0-8229-1150-7&amp;rft.pages=343&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Pittsburgh+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span>&nbsp;:<sup><i>B</i></sup><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.news.pitt.edu/m/FMPro?-db=ma&amp;-lay=a&amp;-format=d.html&amp;id=3379&amp;-Find">&quot;University of Pittsburgh Trustees Approve 2008–09 Budget, Set Tuition Rates&quot;</a>.
